```

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition

# big-code-django-bug-001: Django select_for_update(of) Crash with Annotation Expressions

## Task

Investigate a bug in the Django ORM where combining `select_for_update(of=("self",))` with `values_list()` containing annotation expressions causes an `IndexError` or `AttributeError` crash. Trace the execution path from the user-facing queryset methods through the SQL compiler to identify the root cause.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/django--9e7cc2b6 (mirror of django/django) (Python, ~350K LOC)
- **Category**: Bug Investigation
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Entry Point**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` — `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` method

## Symptom

A Django user writes a queryset that combines `select_for_update(of=("self",))` with `values_list()` including annotation expressions:

```python
from django.db.models import Value, F
from django.db.models.functions import Concat

Person.objects.select_for_update(of=("self",)).values_list(
    Concat(Value("Dr. "), F("name")), "born"
)
```

This crashes with an `AttributeError` on `.target.model` — the ORM attempts to access column metadata on an annotation expression that has no such attribute. Prior to the `values()`/`values_list()` field ordering change, model field columns were always placed first in the SELECT clause. After the change, annotations can appear before model field columns, breaking the `select_for_update(of=...)` table inference logic.

## Requirements

1. Starting from the entry point, trace the execution path to the root cause
2. Identify the specific file(s) and line(s) where the bug originates
3. Explain WHY the bug occurs (not just WHERE)
4. Propose a fix with specific code changes

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```

- path/to/file1.ext — examined for [reason]
- path/to/file2.ext — examined for [reason]
...

...

- **File**: path/to/root_cause.ext
- **Function**: function_name()
- **Line**: ~N
- **Explanation**: [Why this code is buggy]

## Proposed Fix
```diff
- buggy code
+ fixed code
```

```

## Evaluation Criteria

- Root cause identification: Did you find the correct file(s) where the bug originates?
- Call chain accuracy: Did you trace the correct path from symptom to root cause?
- Fix quality: Is the proposed fix correct and minimal?

1. `_get_first_selected_col_from_model(klass_info)` iterates over `klass_info["select_fields"]` (which are indices into `self.select`)
2. For each index, it accesses `self.select[select_index][0].target.model`

142026-03-10T16:47:38.340798agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I understand the key issue. Let me trace through the code:

In `get_select()`:
1. When `self.query.default_cols` is True (normal queryset), `cols` = model columns
2. When `self.query.selected` is not None (values_list with expressions), the code goes into the `else` branch at line 279

The `klass_info["select_fields"]` is set at lines 262-267:
```python
klass_info = {
    "model": self.query.model,
    "select_fields": list(
        range(
            len(self.query.extra_select),
            len(self.query.extra_select) + len(cols),
        )
    ),
}
```

This sets `select_fields` to indices `[len(extra_select), len(extra_select)+1, ..., len(extra_select)+len(cols)-1]`.

But then when `self.query.selected` is not None (the `values_list()` with expressions case), the `selected` list is built differently - it iterates over `self.query.selected.items()` and can include annotation expressions (like `Concat(Value("Dr. "), F("name"))`) in any order.

The key problem: `klass_info["select_fields"]` is computed based on `cols` (the model columns), but the actual position of those columns in `self.select` depends on how `selected` is built.

When `self.query.selected` is None (normal case), the `selected` list is:
```python
[
    *(extra_select items),
    *((None, col) for col in cols),  # model columns at positions len(extra_select) to len(extra_select)+len(cols)-1
    *(annotation_select items),
]
```

So `klass_info["select_fields"]` = `[len(extra_select), ..., len(extra_select)+len(cols)-1]` is correct.

But when `self.query.selected` is not None (values_list with expressions), the `selected` list is built from `self.query.selected.items()` which can have annotations BEFORE model columns. In this case, the `klass_info["select_fields"]` is still comput

2. In `values_list()`, `Concat(...)` has `resolve_expression`, so it gets a generated alias like `concat1`
3. `_fields = ["concat1", "born"]`
4. `expressions = {"concat1": Concat(...)}`
5. `clone = self._values("concat1", "born", concat1=Concat(...))`
6. In `_values()`, `clone.annotate(concat1=Concat(...))` is called first, then `clone.query.set_values(("concat1", "born"))`

7. In `set_values(("concat1", "born"))`:
   - `self.annotations` now contains `concat1` (from the annotate call)
   - `self.annotation_select` contains `concat1` (it's visible)
   - For field `"concat1"`: it's in `self.annotation_select`, so `selected["concat1"] = "concat1"` (a string reference)
   - For field `"born"`: it's not in extra or annotations, so `selected["born"] = 0` (integer, index into field_names), `field_names = ["born"]`
   - `self.selected = {"concat1": "concat1", "born": 0}`

8. In `get_select()` in compiler.py:
   - `self.query.default_cols` is False (set in `set_values` at line 2510)
   - `cols = self.query.select` (the model columns added by `add_fields(["born"], True)`)
   - `cols` contains the `Col` for `born` field
   - `klass_info = {"model": Person, "select_fields": [len(extra_select), ..., len(extra_select)+len(cols)-1]}`
   - Since there's no extra_select, `klass_info["select_fields"] = [0]` (just one column: `born`)

9. Then `selected` is built from `self.query.selected.items()`:
   - `self.query.selected = {"concat1": "concat1", "born": 0}`
   - For `"concat1"`: `expression = "concat1"`

I am thinking...: Now I have a complete picture. Let me trace through the exact bug scenario:

**Scenario**: `Person.objects.select_for_update(of=("self",)).values_list(Concat(Value("Dr. "), F("name")), "born")`

**Step 1: `values_list()` call**
- `Concat(Value("Dr. "), F("name"))` has `resolve_expression`, so it gets alias `concat1`
- `_fields = ["concat1", "born"]`
- `expressions = {"concat1": Concat(...)}`
- Calls `self._values("concat1", "born", concat1=Concat(...))`

**Step 2: `_values()` call**
- `clone.annotate(concat1=Concat(...))` → adds `concat1` to `clone.query.annotations` and `clone.query.annotation_select`
- `clone.query.set_values(("concat1", "born"))`

**Step 3: `set_values(("concat1", "born"))` in `sql/query.py`**
- `self.annotations` contains `concat1`
- `self.annotation_select` contains `concat1`
- For `"concat1"`: it's in `self.annotation_select` → `selected["concat1"] = "concat1"` (string reference)
- For `"born"`: not in extra or annotations → `selected["born"] = 0` (integer, index into field_names), `field_names = ["born"]`
- `self.default_cols = False` (set at line 2510)
- `self.add_fields(["born"], True)` → adds `born` to `self.select` (the query's select list)
- `self.selected = {"concat1": "concat1", "born": 0}`

**Step 4: `get_select()` in `compiler.py`**
- `self.query.default_cols` is False
- `cols = self.query.select` = `[Col("born")]` (one column)
- `klass_info = {"model": Person, "select_fields": [0]}` (range(0, 0+1) = [0])
  - This assumes `born` column is at position 0 in `selected`
- `self.query.selected is not None`, so the `else` branch is taken:
  - For `"concat1"`: `expression = "concat1"` (string) → `expression = self.query.annotations["concat1"]` = `Concat(...)`
  - For `"born"`: `expression = 0` (int) → `expression = cols[0]` =

**Root Cause Summary:**
In `get_select()` (compiler.py ~L259-268), `klass_info["select_fields"]` is computed as `range(len(extra_select), len(extra_select)+len(cols))`. This assumes model columns appear at positions `len(extra_select)` through `len(extra_select)+len(cols)-1` in `selected`.

- When `self.query.selected is None` (normal case): `selected = [extra_select, model_cols, annotations]` — assumption holds ✓
- When `self.query.selected is not None` (values_list with expressions): `selected` is built from `self.query.selected.items()` in insertion order. Annotations can appear BEFORE model columns (e.g., `{"concat1": "concat1", "born": 0}`), so `klass_info["select_fields"] = [0]` points to `Concat(...)` instead of `Col("born")`.

Then in `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` and `_get_parent_klass_info()`, `self.select[0][0].target.model` raises `AttributeError` because `Concat` has no `.target` attribute.

**Proposed Fix** (compiler.py, `get_select()`, else branch ~L279-290):
```python
else:
    se

import os

# The fix: replace lines 279-290 in the original file
# Original block (lines 279-290):
original_block = '''        else:
            for alias, expression in self.query.selected.items():
                # Reference to an annotation.
                if isinstance(expression, str):
                    expression = self.query.annotations[expression]
                # Reference to a column.
                elif isinstance(expression, int):
                    expression = cols[expression]
                # ColPairs cannot be aliased.
                if isinstance(expression, ColPairs):
                    alias = None
                selected.append((alias, expression))'''

# Fixed block:
fixed_block = '''        else:
            select_fields = []
            for alias, expression in self.query.selected.items():
                # Reference to an annotation.
                if isinstance(expression, str):
                    expression = self.query.annotations[expression]
                # Reference to a column.
                elif isinstance(expression, int):
                    select_fields.append(len(selected))
                    expression = cols[expression]
                # ColPairs cannot be aliased.
                if isinstance(expression, ColPairs):
                    alias = None
                selected.append((alias, expression))
            if klass_info is not None:
                klass_info["select_fields"] = select_fields'''

## Summary

**2. `/workspace/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`** — Fixed source file

---

### The Bug

In `get_select()` (`compiler.py`, lines 259–290), `klass_info["select_fields"]` is pre-computed as `range(len(extra_select), len(extra_select) + len(cols))` — assuming model columns occupy a fixed contiguous block starting at position `len(extra_select)` in the final `selected` list.

This assumption holds for the normal queryset path (`self.query.selected is None`), where `selected` is built as `[extra_select, model_cols, annotations]`.

It **breaks** for the `values_list()` path (`self.query.selected is not None`), where `selected` is built from `self.query.selected.items()` in insertion order. When annotation expressions appear before model columns (e.g., `values_list(Concat(...), "born")`), `klass_info["select_fields"] = [0]` points to the `Concat(...)` expression instead of `Col("born")`.

When `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` later calls `self.select[0][0].target.model`, it hits `Concat` which has no `.target` attribute → **`AttributeError`**.

### The Fix (4 lines added)

In the `else` branch of `get_select()`, track the actual positions of model-column references as `selected` is built, then overwrite `klass_info["select_fields"]` with the correct positions:

```python
        else:
            select_fields = []          # ← NEW
            for alias, expression in self.query.selected.items():
... (truncated)

### The fix in brief

**Root cause**: In `get_select()` (`compiler.py` lines 259–268), `klass_info["select_fields"]` is pre-computed as `range(len(extra_select), len(extra_select)+len(cols))` — a fixed offset that assumes model columns always appear first in `selected`. When `values_list()` with annotation expressions is used, annotations can appear *before* model columns in `selected`, making the pre-computed indices point to annotation expressions instead of `Col` objects.

**Fix**: In the `else` branch (the `values()`/`values_list()` path), track the actual positions of model-column references as `selected` is built, then overwrite `klass_info["select_fields"]` with the correct positions:

```python
        else:
            select_fields = []                          # track real positions
            for alias, expression in self.query.selected.items():
                if isinstance(expression, str):
                    expression = self.query.annotations[expression]
                elif isinstance(expression, int):
                    select_fields.append(len(selected)) # record actual position
         
... (truncated)

When `self.query.selected is not None`:\n- `cols` is set to `self.query.select` (line 258)\n- `klass_info` is set based on `cols` (lines 259-268)\n- `selected` is built from `self.query.selected.items()` (line 280)\n\nThe `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` = `range(len(extra_select), len(extra_select)+len(cols))` is computed BEFORE `selected` is built. This range assumes that model columns appear at positions `len(extra_select)` through `len(extra_select)+len(cols)-1` in `selected`.\n\nBut when `self.query.selected is not None`, the `selected` list is built from `self.query.selected.items()`, which can have annotations BEFORE model columns. So the actual positions of model columns in `selected` (and thus `self.select`) may not match `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]`.\n\nThis is the root cause of the bug!\n\nNow let me look at how `self.query.selected` is populated to understand the full picture.\n"

  "file_text": "## Files Examined\n- `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py` \u2014 entry point; contains `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` and `get_select()`\n- `django/db/models/sql/query.py` \u2014 contains `set_values()` which populates `query.selected`\n- `django/db/models/query.py` \u2014 contains `values_list()` and `_values()` which drive the queryset API\n- `tests/select_for_update/tests.py` \u2014 existing tests for `select_for_update(of=...)` with `values_list()`\n- `tests/select_for_update/models.py` \u2014 model definitions (`Person`, `City`, etc.)\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`  \n   `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()` (line ~1440) and `_get_parent_klass_info()` (line ~1424) both do `self.select[select_index][0].target.model`, crashing with `AttributeError` when `self.select[select_index][0]` is an annotation expression (e.g. `Concat`) that has no `.target` attribute.\n\n2. **Called from**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`  \n   `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` (line ~1473) calls `_get_first_selected_col_from_model(klass_info)` for `name == \"self\"`.\n\n3. **Called from**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`  \n   `as_sql()` (line ~884) calls `self.get_select_for_update_of_arguments()`.\n\n4. **Bug triggered by**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`  \n   `get_select()` (lines 259\u2013290) \u2014 `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` is computed with a fixed offset that assumes model columns always appear at positions `[len(extra_select), ..., len(extra_select)+len(cols)-1]` in `selected`. This assumption breaks when `self.query.selected is not None` (i.e. when `values()`/`values_list()` is used with annotation expressions), because annotations can appear before model columns in the `selected` list.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`\n- **Function**: `get_select()`\n- **Lines**: ~259\u2013290\n- **Explanation**:\n\n  `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` is set unconditionally (lines 262\u2013267) as:\n  ```python\n  list(range(len(self.query.extra_select), len(self.query.extra_select) + len(cols)))\n  ```\n  This encodes the assumption that model columns occupy a contiguous block starting at `len(extra_select)` in the final `selected` list.\n\n  That assumption holds when `self.query.selected is None` (the normal queryset path), because `selected` is built as:\n  ```python\n  [extra_select items, model cols, annotation items]\n  ```\n  so model columns are indeed at positions `len(extra_select)` through `len(extra_select)+len(cols)-1`.\n\n  However, when `self.query.selected is not None` (the `values()`/`values_list()` path), `selected` is built by iterating `self.query.selected.items()` in insertion order. When the user writes:\n  ```python\n  Person.objects.select_for_update(of=(\"self\",)).values_list(\n      Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\")), \"born\"\n  )\n  ```\n  `set_values()` in `sql/query.py` produces:\n  ```python\n  self.selected = {\"concat1\": \"concat1\", \"born\": 0}\n  ```\n  (annotation alias `\"concat1\"` first, then model-column integer index `0` for `\"born\"`).\n\n  So `selected` becomes:\n  ```python\n  [(\"concat1\", Concat(...)),   # position 0 \u2014 annotation expression\n   (\"born\",    Col(\"born\"))]   # position 1 \u2014 model column\n  ```\n  But `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` is still `[0]` (computed before `selected` is built), pointing at position 0 \u2014 which is the `Concat(...)` annotation, not a model column.\n\n  When `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` later calls `_get_first_selected_col_from_model()`:\n  ```python\n  for select_index in klass_info[\"select_fields\"]:   # [0]\n      if self.select[select_index][0].target.model == concrete_model:\n  ```\n  `self.select[0][0]` is `Concat(...)`, which has no `.target` attribute \u2192 **`AttributeError`**.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe fix is in `get_select()` in `django/db/models/sql/compiler.py`. When `self.query.selected is not None`, track the actual positions of model-column references (integer values in `self.query.selected`) as `selected` is built, then overwrite `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` with those positions.\n\n```diff\n--- a/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n+++ b/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n@@ -279,10 +279,16 @@ class SQLCompiler:\n         else:\n             for alias, expression in self.query.selected.items():\n                 # Reference to an annotation.\n                 if isinstance(expression, str):\n                     expression = self.query.annotations[expression]\n                 # Reference to a column.\n                 elif isinstance(expression, int):\n+                    if klass_info is not None:\n+                        klass_info.setdefault(\"_select_fields_tmp\", []).append(\n+                            len(selected)\n+                        )\n                     expression = cols[expression]\n                 # ColPairs cannot be aliased.\n                 if isinstance(expression, ColPairs):\n                     alias = None\n                 selected.append((alias, expression))\n+            if klass_info is not None and \"_select_fields_tmp\" in klass_info:\n+                klass_info[\"select_fields\"] = klass_info.pop(\"_select_fields_tmp\")\n```\n\nA cleaner version of the same fix (preferred):\n\n```diff\n--- a/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n+++ b/django/db/models/sql/compiler.py\n@@ -279,9 +279,14 @@ class SQLCompiler:\n         else:\n+            select_fields = []\n             for alias, expression in self.query.selected.items():\n                 # Reference to an annotation.\n                 if isinstance(expression, str):\n                     expression = self.query.annotations[expression]\n                 # Reference to a column.\n                 elif isinstance(expression, int):\n+                    select_fields.append(len(selected))\n                     expression = cols[expression]\n                 # ColPairs cannot be aliased.\n                 if isinstance(expression, ColPairs):\n                     alias = None\n                 selected.append((alias, expression))\n+            if klass_info is not None:\n+                klass_info[\"select_fields\"] = select_fields\n```\n\nThis replaces the stale pre-computed `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` (which assumed model columns come first) with the actual positions of model columns in the `selected` list as built for the `values()`/`values_list()` path.\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Full Execution Trace\n\n**1. User calls `values_list(Concat(...), \"born\")`** (`django/db/models/query.py`, line 1369)\n\n`values_list()` detects that `Concat(Value(\"Dr. \"), F(\"name\"))` has `resolve_expression`, so it generates a synthetic alias `concat1` and calls:\n```python\nclone = self._values(\"concat1\", \"born\", concat1=Concat(...))\n```\n\n**2. `_values()` annotates and calls `set_values()`** (`query.py`, line 1355)\n\n```python\nclone = clone.annotate(concat1=Concat(...))   # adds to query.annotations + annotation_select\nclone.query.set_values((\"concat1\", \"born\"))\n```\n\n**3. `set_values()` builds `query.selected`** (`sql/query.py`, line 2492)\n\nBecause `self.annotations` is non-empty, the `else` branch at line 2509 runs:\n- `\"concat1\"` is in `annotation_select` \u2192 `selected[\"concat1\"] = \"concat1\"` (string ref)\n- `\"born\"` is a plain field \u2192 `selected[\"born\"] = 0` (integer index into `field_names`)\n- `self.default_cols = False`\n- `self.add_fields([\"born\"], True)` \u2192 `self.select = [Col(\"born\")]`\n- `self.selected = {\"concat1\": \"concat1\", \"born\": 0}`\n\n**4. `get_select()` computes `klass_info` with wrong `select_fields`** (`compiler.py`, line 230)\n\n```python\ncols = self.query.select   # [Col(\"born\")]\nklass_info = {\n    \"model\": Person,\n    \"select_fields\": [0],   # \u2190 WRONG: assumes Col(\"born\") is at position 0\n}\n```\n\nThen the `else` branch (line 279) builds `selected` from `self.query.selected.items()`:\n```\nposition 0: (\"concat1\", Concat(...))   \u2190 annotation, NOT a model column\nposition 1: (\"born\",    Col(\"born\"))   \u2190 model column, but klass_info says it's at 0\n```\n\n`self.select` ends up as:\n```\n[0]: (Concat(...), sql, \"concat1\")\n[1]: (Col(\"born\"), sql, \"born\")\n```\n\n**5. `get_select_for_update_of_arguments()` crashes** (`compiler.py`, line 1405)\n\nFor `name = \"self\"`, it calls `_get_first_selected_col_from_model(klass_info)`:\n```python\nfor select_index in [0]:                          # from klass_info[\"select_fields\"]\n    self.select[0][0].target.model                # self.select[0][0] is Concat(...)\n    # AttributeError: 'Concat' object has no attribute 'target'\n```\n\n### Why the Fix Works\n\nBy tracking `select_fields` during the `else` branch loop \u2014 appending `len(selected)` (the current position) whenever an integer reference is encountered \u2014 we record the true positions of model columns in `selected`. After the loop, we overwrite `klass_info[\"select_fields\"]` with these correct positions.\n\nFor the example above, `select_fields` would be `[1]` (Col(\"born\") is at position 1), so `_get_first_selected_col_from_model` would correctly examine `self.select[1][0]` = `Col(\"born\")`, which has `.target.model == Person`, and return it successfully.\n\nThe fix is minimal (4 lines added in the `else` branch of `get_select()`) and does not affect the `self.query.selected is None` path at all.\n",
